<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Urewe">Urewe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Urewe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Urewe#Chronology" title="Urewe">Urewe § Chronology</a></div>
<p>The <b>Urewe</b> culture developed and spread in and around the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> region of Africa during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Iron_Age" title="African Iron Age">African Iron Age</a>. The culture's earliest dated artifacts are located in the <a href="/wiki/Kagera_Region" title="Kagera Region">Kagera Region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, and it extended as far west as the <a href="/wiki/Kivu" title="Kivu">Kivu</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, as far east as the <a href="/wiki/Nyanza_Province" title="Nyanza Province">Nyanza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Province_(Kenya)" title="Western Province (Kenya)">Western</a> provinces of <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, and north into <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>. Sites from the Urewe culture date from the Early Iron Age, from the 5th century BC to the 6th century AD.
</p><p>The origins of the Urewe culture are ultimately in the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> originating in Cameroon. Research into early Iron Age civilizations in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> has been undertaken concurrently with studies on African linguistics on Bantu expansion. The Urewe culture may correspond to the Eastern subfamily of Bantu languages, spoken by the descendants of the first wave of Bantu peoples to settle East Africa. At first sight, Urewe seems to be a fully developed civilization recognizable through its distinctive, stylish earthenware and highly technical and sophisticated iron working techniques. Given our current level of knowledge, neither seems to have developed or altered for nearly 2,000 years. However, minor local variations in the ceramic ware can be observed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Urewe is the name of the site in Kenya brought to prominence through the publication in 1948 of <a href="/wiki/Mary_Leakey" title="Mary Leakey">Mary Leakey</a>'s archaeological findings. She described the early Iron Age period in the Great Lakes region in Central East Africa around Lake Victoria.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Madagascar_and_Merina">Madagascar and Merina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Madagascar and Merina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madagascar" title="History of Madagascar">History of Madagascar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merina_people#History" title="Merina people">Merina people § History</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_(edit).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1893" data-file-width="2846" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg/220px-The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg/330px-The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg/440px-The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_%28edit%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Queen%27s_Ordinary_Style_of_Appearing_in_Public_(edit).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queen <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_I" title="Ranavalona I">Ranavalona I</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> was apparently first settled by <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a> speakers from <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> before the 6th century AD and subsequently by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> speakers from the east African mainland in the 6th or 7th century, according to archaeological and linguistic data. The Austronesians introduced <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> cultivation, and the Bantu speakers introduced cattle and other farming practices. About the year 1000, Arab and Indian trade settlement were started in northern Madagascar to exploit the Indian Ocean trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> By the 14th century, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was introduced on the island by traders. Madagascar functioned in the East African medieval period as a contact port for the other Swahili seaport city-states such as <a href="/wiki/Sofala" title="Sofala">Sofala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_Sultanate" title="Kilwa Sultanate">Kilwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Several kingdoms emerged after the 15th century: the <a href="/wiki/Sakalava_people" title="Sakalava people">Sakalava Kingdom</a> (16th century) on the west coast, Tsitambala Kingdom (17th century) on the east coast, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merina" title="Merina">Merina</a> (15th century) in the central highlands. By the 19th century, Merina controlled the whole island. In 1500, the Portuguese were the first Europeans on the island, raiding the trading settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELye2002242–243_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELye2002242–243-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p><p>The British and later the French arrived. During the latter part of the 17th century, Madagascar was a popular transit point for <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radama_I_of_Madagascar" title="Radama I of Madagascar">Radama I</a> (1810–1828) invited Christian <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> in the early 19th century. Queen <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_I" title="Ranavalona I">Ranavalona I</a> "the Cruel" (1828–1861) banned the practice of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> in the kingdom, and an estimated 150,000 Christians perished. Under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radama_II_of_Madagascar" title="Radama II of Madagascar">Radama II</a> (1861–1863), Madagascar took a French orientation, with great commercial concession given to the French. In 1895, in the second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_War" title="Franco-Hova War">Franco-Hova War</a>, the French invaded Madagascar, taking over <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana" title="Antsiranana">Antsiranana</a> (Diego Suarez) and declaring Madagascar a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELye2002242–243_245-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELye2002242–243-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lake_Plateau_states_and_empires">Lake Plateau states and empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Lake Plateau states and empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Buganda" title="History of Buganda">History of Buganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karagwe_District#History" title="Karagwe District">Karagwe District § History</a></div>
<p>Between the 14th and 15th centuries, large Southeast African kingdoms and states emerged, such as the <a href="/wiki/Buganda" title="Buganda">Buganda</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roland_Oliver_1800._pp._24–25_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roland_Oliver_1800._pp._24–25-246">[246]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karagwe" title="Karagwe">Karagwe</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roland_Oliver_1800._pp._24–25_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roland_Oliver_1800._pp._24–25-246">[246]</a></sup> Kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span id=".F0.9D.97.98.F0.9D.97.BA.F0.9D.97.BD.F0.9D.97.B6.F0.9D.97.BF.F0.9D.97.B2_.F0.9D.97.BC.F0.9D.97.B3_.F0.9D.97.B8.F0.9D.97.B6.F0.9D.98.81.F0.9D.97.AE.F0.9D.97.BF.F0.9D.97.AE"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="𝗘𝗺𝗽𝗶𝗿𝗲_𝗼𝗳_𝗸𝗶𝘁𝗮𝗿𝗮">𝗘𝗺𝗽𝗶𝗿𝗲 𝗼𝗳 𝗸𝗶𝘁𝗮𝗿𝗮</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: 𝗘𝗺𝗽𝗶𝗿𝗲 𝗼𝗳 𝗸𝗶𝘁𝗮𝗿𝗮">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Kitara#Founding" title="Empire of Kitara">Empire of Kitara § Founding</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bunyoro#History" title="Bunyoro">Bunyoro § History</a></div>
<p>By 1000 AD, numerous states had arisen on the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Plateau" title="East African Plateau">Lake Plateau</a> among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_(Africa)" title="Great Lakes (Africa)">Great Lakes</a> of East Africa. Cattle herding, cereal growing, and banana cultivation were the economic mainstays of these states. The <a href="/wiki/Ntusi" title="Ntusi">Ntusi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bigo_bya_Mugenyi" title="Bigo bya Mugenyi">Bigo</a> earthworks are representative of one of the first states, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bunyoro_kingdom" title="Bunyoro kingdom">Bunyoro kingdom</a>, which oral tradition stipulates was part of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Kitara" title="Empire of Kitara">Empire of Kitara</a> that dominated the whole Lakes region. A <a href="/wiki/Luo_peoples" title="Luo peoples">Luo</a> ethnic elite, from the Babito clan, ruled over the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu-speaking</a> <a href="/wiki/Nyoro_people" title="Nyoro people">Nyoro people</a>. The society was essentially Nyoro in its culture, based on the evidence from pottery, settlement patterns, and economic specialization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._122–123_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._122–123-248">[248]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Babito clan claim legitimacy by being descended from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bachwezi" title="Bachwezi">Bachwezi</a> clan, who were said to have ruled the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Kitara" title="Empire of Kitara">Empire of Kitara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Buganda">Buganda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Buganda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Buganda" title="History of Buganda">History of Buganda</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Kabaka_of_Buganda" title="Kabaka of Buganda">Kabaka of Buganda</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buganda_kingdom" title="Buganda kingdom">Buganda kingdom</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Kimera_of_Buganda" title="Kimera of Buganda">Kato Kimera</a> around the 14th century AD. Kato Kintu may have migrated to the northwest of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> as early as 1000 BC. Buganda was ruled by the <i><a href="/wiki/Kabaka_of_Buganda" title="Kabaka of Buganda">kabaka</a></i> with a <i>bataka</i> composed of the clan heads. Over time, the <i>kabakas</i> diluted the authority of the <i>bataka</i>, with Buganda becoming a centralized monarchy. By the 16th century, Buganda was engaged in expansion but had a serious rival in <a href="/wiki/Bunyoro" title="Bunyoro">Bunyoro</a>. By the 1870s, Buganda was a wealthy nation-state. The <i>kabaka</i> ruled with his <i>Lukiko</i> (council of ministers). Buganda had a naval fleet of a hundred vessels, each manned by thirty men. Buganda supplanted Bunyoro as the most important state in the region. However, by the early 20th century, Buganda became a province of the British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uganda_Protectorate" title="Uganda Protectorate">Uganda Protectorate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELye2002121–122_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELye2002121–122-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Rwanda">Rwanda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Rwanda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Rwanda#Pre-colonization" title="Kingdom of Rwanda">Kingdom of Rwanda § Pre-colonization</a></div>
<p>Southeast of Bunyoro, near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Kivu" title="Lake Kivu">Lake Kivu</a> at the bottom of the western rift, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Rwanda" title="Kingdom of Rwanda">Kingdom of Rwanda</a> was founded, perhaps during the 17th century. <a href="/wiki/Tutsi" title="Tutsi">Tutsi</a> (BaTutsi) pastoralists formed the elite, with a king called the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Rwanda" title="King of Rwanda">mwami</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">Hutu</a> (BaHutu) were farmers. Both groups spoke the same language, but there were strict social norms against marrying each other and interaction. According to oral tradition, the Kingdom of Rwanda was founded by Mwami Ruganzu II (Ruganzu Ndori) (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1600</span> – 1624), with his capital near <a href="/wiki/Kigali" title="Kigali">Kigali</a>. It took 200 years to attain a truly centralized kingdom under Mwami <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kigeli_IV_of_Rwanda" title="Kigeli IV of Rwanda">Kigeli IV</a> (Kigeri Rwabugiri) (1840–1895). Subjugation of the Hutu proved more difficult than subduing the Tutsi. The last Tutsi chief gave up to Mwami <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutara_II_of_Rwanda" title="Mutara II of Rwanda">Mutara II</a> (Mutara Rwogera) (1802–1853) in 1852, but the last Hutu holdout was conquered in the 1920s by Mwami <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuhi_V_of_Rwanda" title="Yuhi V of Rwanda">Yuhi V</a> (Yuli Musinga) (1896–1931).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Burundi">Burundi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Burundi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Burundi#History" title="Kingdom of Burundi">Kingdom of Burundi § History</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Kings_of_Burundi" title="List of Kings of Burundi">List of Kings of Burundi</a></div>
<p>South of the Kingdom of Rwanda was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burundian_monarchy" title="Burundian monarchy">Kingdom of Burundi</a>. It was founded by the Tutsi chief <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ntare_I_Kivimira_Savuyimba_Semunganzashamba_Rushatsi_Cambarantama" title="Ntare I Kivimira Savuyimba Semunganzashamba Rushatsi Cambarantama">Ntare Rushatsi</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1657</span> – 1705). Like Rwanda, Burundi was built on cattle raised by Tutsi pastoralists, crops from Hutu farmers, conquest, and political innovations. Under Mwami <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ntare_IV_Rutaganzwa_Rugamba" title="Ntare IV Rutaganzwa Rugamba">Ntare Rugaamba</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1795</span> – 1852), Burundi pursued an aggressive expansionist policy, one based more on diplomacy than force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maravi">Maravi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Maravi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maravi" title="Maravi">Maravi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="828" data-file-width="747" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg/220px-Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg/330px-Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg/440px-Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maravi_Kingdom_map_c._1650s.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maravi Kingdom</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maravi" title="Maravi">Maravi</a> claimed descent from Karonga (<i>kalonga</i>), who took that title as king. The Maravi connected Central Africa to the east coastal trade, with <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a> Kilwa. By the 17th century, the Maravi Empire encompassed all the area between <a href="/wiki/Lake_Malawi" title="Lake Malawi">Lake Malawi</a> and the mouth of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zambezi_River" title="Zambezi River">Zambezi River</a>. The <i>karonga</i> was Mzura, who did much to extend the empire. Mzura made a pact with the Portuguese to establish a 4,000-man army to attack the <a href="/wiki/Shona_people" title="Shona people">Shona</a> in return for aid in defeating his rival Lundi, a chief of the Zimba. In 1623, he turned on the Portuguese and assisted the Shona. In 1640, he welcomed back the Portuguese for trade. The Maravi Empire did not long survive the death of Mzura. By the 18th century, it had broken into its previous polities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991164–165_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991164–165-253">[253]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Africa_2">West Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: West Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_West_Africa" title="History of West Africa">History of West Africa</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sahelian_empires_and_states">Sahelian empires and states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Sahelian empires and states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sahelian_kingdoms#History_of_Sahel_kingdoms" title="Sahelian kingdoms">Sahelian kingdoms § History of Sahel kingdoms</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire#Origin" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire § Origin</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Serer_history" title="Serer history">Serer history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Ghana_Empire.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="451" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/The_Ghana_Empire.svg/220px-The_Ghana_Empire.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/The_Ghana_Empire.svg/330px-The_Ghana_Empire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/The_Ghana_Empire.svg/440px-The_Ghana_Empire.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Ghana_Empire.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ghana Empire</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">Ghana Empire</a> may have been an established kingdom as early as the 8th century AD, founded among the <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">Soninke</a> by Dinge Cisse. Ghana was first mentioned by Arab geographer Al-Farazi in the late 8th century. Ghana was inhabited by urban dwellers and rural farmers. The urban dwellers were the administrators of the empire, who were Muslims, and the <i>Ghana</i> (king), who practiced traditional religion. Two towns existed, one where the Muslim administrators and Berber-Arabs lived, which was connected by a stone-paved road to the king's residence. The rural dwellers lived in villages, which joined into broader polities that pledged loyalty to the <i>Ghana.</i> The <i>Ghana</i> was viewed as divine, and his physical well-being reflected on the whole society. Ghana converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> around 1050, after conquering <a href="/wiki/Aoudaghost" title="Aoudaghost">Aoudaghost</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Ghana Empire grew wealthy by taxing the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> that linked <a href="/wiki/Tiaret" title="Tiaret">Tiaret</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sijilmasa" title="Sijilmasa">Sijilmasa</a> to Aoudaghost. Ghana controlled access to the goldfields of <a href="/wiki/Bambouk" title="Bambouk">Bambouk</a>, southeast of <a href="/wiki/Koumbi_Saleh" title="Koumbi Saleh">Koumbi Saleh</a>. A percentage of salt and gold going through its territory was taken. The empire was not involved in production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the 11th century, Ghana was in decline. It was once thought that the sacking of Koumbi Saleh by Berbers under the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid dynasty</a> in 1076 was the cause. This is no longer accepted. Several alternative explanations are cited. One important reason is the transfer of the gold trade east to the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Taghaza" title="Taghaza">Taghaza</a> Trail, and Ghana's consequent economic decline. Another reason cited is political instability through rivalry among the different hereditary polities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-256">[256]</a></sup>
The empire came to an end in 1230, when <a href="/wiki/Takrur" title="Takrur">Takrur</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> took over the capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991173–174_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991173–174-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mali">Mali</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Mali">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire#Pre-imperial_Mali" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire § Pre-imperial Mali</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keita_Dynasty" title="Keita Dynasty">Keita Dynasty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MALI_empire_map.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="994" data-file-width="1580" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/220px-MALI_empire_map.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/330px-MALI_empire_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MALI_empire_map.PNG/440px-MALI_empire_map.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MALI_empire_map.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mali Empire at its greatest extent</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> began in the 13th century AD, when a <a href="/wiki/Mand%C3%A9_peoples" title="Mandé peoples">Mande</a> (Mandingo) leader, <a href="/wiki/Sundiata_Keita" title="Sundiata Keita">Sundiata</a> (Lord Lion) of the Keita clan, defeated <a href="/wiki/Soumaoro_Kant%C3%A9" title="Soumaoro Kanté">Soumaoro Kanté</a>, king of the <a href="/wiki/Susu_people" title="Susu people">Sosso</a> or southern <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">Soninke</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kirina" title="Battle of Kirina">Battle of Kirina</a> in <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1235</span>. Sundiata continued his conquest from the fertile forests and Niger Valley, east to the Niger Bend, north into the Sahara, and west to the Atlantic Ocean, absorbing the remains of the Ghana Empire. Sundiata took on the title of <i><a href="/wiki/Mansa_(title)" title="Mansa (title)">mansa</a></i>. He established the capital of his empire at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niani,_Mali" title="Niani, Mali">Niani</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the salt and gold trade continued to be important to the Mali Empire, agriculture and pastoralism was also critical. The growing of <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, and rice was a vital function. On the northern borders of the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>, grazing cattle, sheep, goats, and camels were major activities. Mande society was organize around the village and land. A cluster of villages was called a <i>kafu</i>, ruled by a <i>farma</i>. The <i>farma</i> paid tribute to the <i>mansa</i>. A dedicated army of elite cavalry and infantry maintained order, commanded by the royal court. A formidable force could be raised from tributary regions, if necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._83–87_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._83–87-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conversion to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was a gradual process. The power of the <i>mansa</i> depended on upholding traditional beliefs and a spiritual foundation of power. Sundiata initially kept Islam at bay. Later <i>mansas</i> were devout Muslims but still acknowledged traditional <a href="/wiki/Deity" title="Deity">deities</a> and took part in traditional rituals and festivals, which were important to the Mande. Islam became a court religion under Sundiata's son <a href="/wiki/Uli_I_of_Mali" title="Uli I of Mali">Uli I</a> (1225–1270). <i>Mansa</i> Uli made a pilgrimage to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, becoming recognized within the Muslim world. The court was staffed with literate Muslims as secretaries and accountants. Muslim traveller <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a> left vivid descriptions of the empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._83–87_260-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._83–87-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mali reached the peak of its power and extent in the 14th century, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musa_I_of_Mali" title="Musa I of Mali"><i>Mansa</i> Musa</a> (1312–1337) made his famous <i><a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">hajj</a></i> to Mecca with 500 slaves, each holding a bar of gold worth 500 mitqals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson197183_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson197183-261">[261]</a></sup> <i>Mansa</i> Musa's <i>hajj</i> devalued gold in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluk Egypt</a> for a decade. He made a great impression on the minds of the Muslim and European world. He invited scholars and architects like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Sahili" title="Al Sahili">Ishal al-Tuedjin</a> (al-Sahili) to further integrate Mali into the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Islamic world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._83–87_260-2"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._83–87-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mali Empire saw an expansion of learning and <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a>. In 1285, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakura_(mansa)" title="Sakura (mansa)">Sakura</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Freedman" title="Freedman">freed slave</a>, usurped the throne. This <i>mansa</i> drove the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a> out of <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> and established it as a center of learning and commerce. The book trade increased, and book copying became a very respectable and profitable profession. Timbuktu and <a href="/wiki/Djenn%C3%A9" title="Djenné">Djenné</a> became important centers of learning within the Islamic world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson197184–85_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson197184–85-262">[262]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the reign of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suleyman_(mansa)" title="Suleyman (mansa)">Mansa Suleyman</a> (1341–1360), Mali began its spiral downward. <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Mossi</a> cavalry raided the exposed southern border. Tuareg harassed the northern border in order to retake Timbuktu. <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> (Fulbe) eroded Mali's authority in the west by establishing the independent <a href="/wiki/Imamate_of_Futa_Toro" title="Imamate of Futa Toro">Imamate of Futa Toro</a>, a successor to the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Takrur" title="Takrur">Takrur</a>. <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">Serer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wolof_Empire" title="Wolof Empire">Wolof</a> alliances were broken. In 1545 to 1546, the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a> took <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niani,_Mali_Empire" title="Niani, Mali Empire">Niani</a>. After 1599, the empire lost the <a href="/wiki/Bambouk" title="Bambouk">Bambouk</a> goldfields and disintegrated into petty polities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._83–87_260-3"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._83–87-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Songhai">Songhai</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Songhai">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire#History" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire § History</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Askiya_Dynasty" title="Askiya Dynasty">Askiya Dynasty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonni_Dynasty" title="Sonni Dynasty">Sonni Dynasty</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="988" data-file-width="1580" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG/220px-SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG/330px-SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG/440px-SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SONGHAI_empire_map.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Songhai Empire, c. 1500</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Songhai_people" title="Songhai people">Songhai people</a> are descended from fishermen on the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Middle Niger River</a>. They established their capital at Kukiya in the 9th century AD and at <a href="/wiki/Gao" title="Gao">Gao</a> in the 12th century. The Songhai speak a <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">Nilo-Saharan language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sonni_Ali" title="Sonni Ali">Sonni Ali</a>, a Songhai, began his conquest by capturing <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> in 1468 from the <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuareg</a>. He extended the empire to the north, deep into the desert, pushed the <a href="/wiki/Mossi_people" title="Mossi people">Mossi</a> further south of the Niger, and expanded southwest to Djenne. His army consisted of cavalry and a fleet of canoes. Sonni Ali was not a Muslim, and he was portrayed negatively by Berber-Arab scholars, especially for attacking Muslim Timbuktu. After his death in 1492, his heirs were deposed by General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Askia_Mohammad_I" title="Askia Mohammad I">Muhammad Ture</a>, a Muslim of Soninke origins<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup>
</p><p>Muhammad Ture (1493–1528) founded the <a href="/wiki/Askiya_Dynasty" title="Askiya Dynasty">Askiya Dynasty</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Askiya" title="Askiya">askiya</a></i> being the title of the king. He consolidated the conquests of Sonni Ali. Islam was used to extend his authority by declaring <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a> on the Mossi, reviving the trans-Saharan trade, and having the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid "shadow" caliph</a> in Cairo declare him as caliph of Sudan. He established Timbuktu as a great center of Islamic learning. Muhammad Ture expanded the empire by pushing the Tuareg north, capturing Aïr in the east, and capturing salt-producing <a href="/wiki/Taghaza" title="Taghaza">Taghaza</a>. He brought the <a href="/wiki/Hausa_Kingdoms" title="Hausa Kingdoms">Hausa states</a> into the Songhay trading network. He further centralized the administration of the empire by selecting administrators from loyal servants and families and assigning them to conquered territories. They were responsible for raising local militias. Centralization made Songhay very stable, even during dynastic disputes. <a href="/wiki/Leo_Africanus" title="Leo Africanus">Leo Africanus</a> left vivid descriptions of the empire under Askiya Muhammad. Askiya Muhammad was deposed by his son in 1528. After much rivalry, Muhammad Ture's last son <a href="/wiki/Askia_Daoud" title="Askia Daoud">Askiya Daoud</a> (1529–1582) assumed the throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1591, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> invaded the Songhai Empire under <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Mansur" title="Ahmad al-Mansur">Ahmad al-Mansur</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saadi_Dynasty" title="Saadi Dynasty">Saadi Dynasty</a> in order to secure the goldfields of the Sahel. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tondibi" title="Battle of Tondibi">Battle of Tondibi</a>, the Songhai army was defeated. The Moroccans captured Djenne, Gao, and Timbuktu, but they were unable to secure the whole region. Askiya Nuhu and the Songhay army regrouped at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dendi_Kingdom" title="Dendi Kingdom">Dendi</a> in the heart of Songhai territory where a spirited guerrilla resistance sapped the resources of the Moroccans, who were dependent upon constant resupply from Morocco. Songhai split into several states during the 17th century.
</p><p>Morocco found its venture unprofitable. The gold trade had been diverted to Europeans on the coast. Most of the trans-Saharan trade was now diverted east to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bornu_Empire" title="Bornu Empire">Bornu</a>. Expensive equipment purchased with gold had to be sent across the Sahara, an unsustainable scenario. The Moroccans who remained married into the population and were referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Arma_people" title="Arma people">Arma</a></i> or <i>Ruma</i>. They established themselves at Timbuktu as a military caste with various fiefs, independent from Morocco. Amid the chaos, other groups began to assert themselves, including the <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> of <a href="/wiki/Futa_Tooro" title="Futa Tooro">Futa Tooro</a> who encroached from the west. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambara_Empire" title="Bambara Empire">Bambara Empire</a>, one of the states that broke from Songhai, sacked Gao. In 1737, the Tuareg massacred the <i>Arma</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns_2007_pp._88–89_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2007_pp._88–89-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Sokoto_Caliphate">Sokoto Caliphate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Sokoto Caliphate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sokoto_Caliphate#History" title="Sokoto Caliphate">Sokoto Caliphate § History</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1130" data-file-width="2280" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png/330px-Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png/495px-Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png/660px-Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scramble-for-Africa-1880-1913-v2.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comparison of Africa in the years 1880 and 1913</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulani</a> were migratory people. They moved from <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> and settled in <a href="/wiki/Futa_Tooro" title="Futa Tooro">Futa Tooro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fouta_Djallon" title="Fouta Djallon">Futa Djallon</a>, and subsequently throughout the rest of West Africa. By the 14th century CE, they had converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. During the 16th century, they established themselves at <a href="/wiki/Macina,_Mali" title="Macina, Mali">Macina</a> in southern <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>. During the 1670s, they declared <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihads</a> on non-Muslims. Several states were formed from these jihadist wars, at Futa Toro, Futa Djallon, Macina, <a href="/wiki/Oualia" title="Oualia">Oualia</a>, and Bundu. The most important of these states was the <a href="/wiki/Sokoto_Caliphate" title="Sokoto Caliphate">Sokoto Caliphate</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fulani_Empire" title="Fulani Empire">Fulani Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the city of <a href="/wiki/Gobir" title="Gobir">Gobir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usman_dan_Fodio" title="Usman dan Fodio">Usman dan Fodio</a> (1754–1817) accused the Hausa leadership of practicing an impure version of Islam and of being morally corrupt. In 1804, he launched the <a href="/wiki/Fulani_War" title="Fulani War">Fulani War</a> as a jihad among a population that was restless about high taxes and discontented with its leaders. Jihad fever swept northern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, with strong support among both the Fulani and the Hausa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Usman created an empire that included parts of northern Nigeria, <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Sokoto" title="Sokoto">Sokoto</a> as its capital. He retired to teach and write and handed the empire to his son <a href="/wiki/Muhammed_Bello" title="Muhammed Bello">Muhammed Bello</a>. The Sokoto Caliphate lasted until 1903 when the British conquered northern Nigeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELye2002188_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELye2002188-268">[268]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_empires_and_states">Forest empires and states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Forest empires and states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Akan_kingdoms_and_emergence_of_Asante_Empire">Akan kingdoms and emergence of Asante Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Akan kingdoms and emergence of Asante Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Akan_people#Origin_and_ethnogenesis" title="Akan people">Akan people § Origin and ethnogenesis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bono_state#Origin" title="Bono state">Bono state § Origin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire#History" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire § History</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Asante" title="List of rulers of Asante">List of rulers of Asante</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kent_wove.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="513" data-file-width="371" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg/180px-Kent_wove.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg/270px-Kent_wove.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Kent_wove.jpg/360px-Kent_wove.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kent_wove.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashanti_people" title="Ashanti people">Ashanti</a> <a href="/wiki/Kente_cloth" title="Kente cloth">Kente cloth</a> patterns</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> speak a <a href="/wiki/Kwa_languages" title="Kwa languages">Kwa language</a>. The speakers of Kwa languages are believed to have come from <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East</a>/<a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>, before settling in the <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> By the 12th century, the Akan Kingdom of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonoman" title="Bonoman">Bonoman</a> (Bono State) was established. During the 13th century, when the gold mines in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> started to dry up, Bonoman and later other Akan states began to rise to prominence as the major players in the Gold trade. It was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonoman" title="Bonoman">Bonoman</a> and other Akan kingdoms like <a href="/wiki/Denkyira" title="Denkyira">Denkyira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akyem" title="Akyem">Akyem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a> which were the predecessors, and later the emergence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_of_Ashanti" title="Empire of Ashanti">Empire of Ashanti</a>. When and how the Ashante got to their present location is debatable. What is known is that by the 17th century an Akan people were identified as living in a state called Kwaaman. The location of the state was north of Lake Bosomtwe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The state's revenue was mainly derived from trading in gold and <a href="/wiki/Kola_nut" title="Kola nut">kola nuts</a> and clearing forest to plant <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>. They built towns between the <a href="/wiki/Pra_River_(Ghana)" title="Pra River (Ghana)">Pra</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ofin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ofin (page does not exist)">Ofin</a> rivers. They formed alliances for defense and paid tribute to <a href="/wiki/Denkyira" title="Denkyira">Denkyira</a> one of the more powerful Akan states at that time along with Adansi and <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a>. During the 16th century, Ashante society experienced sudden changes, including population growth because of cultivation of <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> plants such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> and an increase in the gold trade between the coast and the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the 17th century, <a href="/wiki/Osei_Kofi_Tutu_I" title="Osei Kofi Tutu I">Osei Kofi Tutu I</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1695</span> – 1717), with help of <a href="/wiki/Okomfo_Anokye" title="Okomfo Anokye">Okomfo Anokye</a>, unified what became the Ashante into a confederation with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asante_royal_thrones" title="Asante royal thrones">Golden Stool</a> as a symbol of their unity and spirit. Osei Tutu engaged in a massive territorial expansion. He built up the Ashante army based on the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a>, introducing new organization and turning a disciplined militia into an effective fighting machine.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1701, the Ashante conquered Denkyira, giving them access to the coastal trade with Europeans, especially the Dutch. <a href="/wiki/Opoku_Ware_I" title="Opoku Ware I">Opoku Ware I</a> (1720–1745) engaged in further expansion, adding other southern Akan states to the growing empire. He turned north adding <a href="/wiki/Techiman" title="Techiman">Techiman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banda_Ahenkro" title="Banda Ahenkro">Banda</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gyaaman" title="Gyaaman">Gyaaman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gonja_people" title="Gonja people">Gonja</a>, states on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Volta" title="Black Volta">Black Volta</a>. Between 1744 and 1745, <i>Asantehene</i> Opoku attacked the powerful northern state of Dagomba, gaining control of the important middle Niger trade routes. <a href="/wiki/Kusi_Obodom" title="Kusi Obodom">Kusi Obodom</a> (1750–1764) succeeded Opoku. He solidified all the newly won territories. <a href="/wiki/Osei_Kwadwo" title="Osei Kwadwo">Osei Kwadwo</a> (1777–1803) imposed administrative reforms that allowed the empire to be governed effectively and to continue its military expansion. <a href="/wiki/Osei_Kwame_Panyin" title="Osei Kwame Panyin">Osei Kwame Panyin</a> (1777–1803), Osei Tutu Kwame (1804–1807), and Osei Bonsu (1807–1824) continued territorial consolidation and expansion. The Ashante Empire included all of present-day <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> and large parts of the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Ashantehene</i> inherited his position from his mother. He was assisted at the capital, Kumasi, by a civil service of men talented in trade, diplomacy, and the military, with a head called the <i>Gyaasehene</i>. Men from Arabia, Sudan, and Europe were employed in the civil service, all of them appointed by the <i>Ashantehene</i>. At the capital and in other towns, the <i>ankobia</i> or special police were used as bodyguards to the <i>Ashantehene</i>, as sources of intelligence, and to suppress rebellion. Communication throughout the empire was maintained via a network of well-kept roads from the coast to the middle Niger and linking together other trade cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991240_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991240-272">[272]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>For most of the 19th century, the Ashante Empire remained powerful. It was later destroyed in 1900 by British superior weaponry and organization following the four <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Ashanti_wars" title="Anglo-Ashanti wars">Anglo-Ashanti wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991242_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991242-274">[274]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dahomey">Dahomey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Dahomey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Kingdom_of_Dahomey" title="History of the Kingdom of Dahomey">History of the Kingdom of Dahomey</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Aja_people#History" title="Aja people">Aja people § History</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dahomey_amazon2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="536" data-file-width="819" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Dahomey_amazon2.jpg/280px-Dahomey_amazon2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Dahomey_amazon2.jpg/420px-Dahomey_amazon2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Dahomey_amazon2.jpg/560px-Dahomey_amazon2.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dahomey_amazon2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dahomey_Amazons" title="Dahomey Amazons">Dahomey Amazons</a>, an all-women fighting unit</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">Dahomey Kingdom</a> was founded in the early 17th century when the <a href="/wiki/Aja_people" title="Aja people">Aja people</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Allada" title="Allada">Allada</a> kingdom moved northward and settled among the <a href="/wiki/Fon_people" title="Fon people">Fon</a>. They began to assert their power a few years later. In so doing they established the Kingdom of Dahomey, with its capital at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agbome" title="Agbome">Agbome</a>. King <a href="/wiki/Houegbadja" title="Houegbadja">Houegbadja</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1645</span> – 1685) organized Dahomey into a powerful centralized state. He declared all lands to be owned of the king and subject to taxation. <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">Primogeniture</a> in the kingship was established, neutralizing all input from village chiefs. A "cult of kingship" was established. A captive slave would be sacrificed annually to honor the royal ancestors. During the 1720s, the slave-trading states of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Whydah" title="Kingdom of Whydah">Whydah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allada" title="Allada">Allada</a> were taken, giving Dahomey direct access to the slave coast and trade with Europeans. King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agadja" title="Agadja">Agadja</a> (1708–1740) attempted to end the slave trade by keeping the slaves on plantations producing palm oil, but the European profits on slaves and Dahomey's dependency on <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a> were too great. In 1730, under king Agaja, Dahomey was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">Oyo Empire</a>, and Dahomey had to pay tribute. Taxes on slaves were mostly paid in cowrie shells. During the 19th century, palm oil was the main trading commodity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">France</a> conquered Dahomey during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Franco-Dahomean_War" title="Second Franco-Dahomean War">Second Franco-Dahomean War</a> (1892–1894) and established a colonial government there. Most of the troops who fought against Dahomey were native Africans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Yoruba">Yoruba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Yoruba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Yoruba_people" title="History of the Yoruba people">History of the Yoruba people</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_the_Yoruba_state_of_Oyo" title="List of rulers of the Yoruba state of Oyo">List of rulers of the Yoruba state of Oyo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WestAfrica1625.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="306" data-file-width="498" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/WestAfrica1625.png/280px-WestAfrica1625.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/WestAfrica1625.png/420px-WestAfrica1625.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/WestAfrica1625.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WestAfrica1625.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oyo Empire and surrounding states, c. 1625</div></div></div>
<p>Traditionally, the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba people</a> viewed themselves as the inhabitants of a united empire, in contrast to the situation today, in which "Yoruba" is the cultural-linguistic designation for speakers of a language in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niger%E2%80%93Congo" title="Niger–Congo">Niger–Congo</a> family. The name comes from a <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">Hausa</a> word to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">Oyo Empire</a>. The first Yoruba state was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ife" title="Ife">Ile-Ife</a>, said to have been founded around 1000 AD by a supernatural figure, the first <i>oni</i> <a href="/wiki/Oduduwa" title="Oduduwa">Oduduwa</a>. Oduduwa's sons would be the founders of the different city-states of the Yoruba, and his daughters would become the mothers of the various Yoruba <i>obas</i>, or kings. Yoruba city-states were usually governed by an <i>oba</i> and an <i>iwarefa</i>, a council of chiefs who advised the <i>oba.</i> by the 18th century, the Yoruba city-states formed a loose confederation, with the <i>Oni</i> of Ife as the head and Ife as the capital. As time went on, the individual city-states became more powerful with their <i>obas</i> assuming more powerful spiritual positions and diluting the authority of the <i>Oni</i> of Ife. Rivalry became intense among the city-states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Oyo Empire rose in the 16th century. The Oyo state had been conquered in 1550 by the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Nupe_people" title="Nupe people">Nupe</a>, which was in possession of cavalry, an important tactical advantage. The <i>alafin</i> (king) of Oyo was sent into exile. After returning, <i>Alafin</i> <a href="/wiki/Orompoto" title="Orompoto">Orompoto</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1560</span> – 1580) built up an army based on heavily armed cavalry and long-service troops. This made them invincible in combat on the northern grasslands and in the thinly wooded forests. By the end of the 16th century, Oyo had added the western region of the Niger to the hills of Togo, the Yoruba of <a href="/wiki/Ketu_(Benin)" title="Ketu (Benin)">Ketu</a>, Dahomey, and the Fon nation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_256-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-256">[256]</a></sup>
</p><p>A governing council served the empire, with clear executive divisions. Each acquired region was assigned a local administrator. Families served in king-making capacities. Oyo, as a northern Yoruba kingdom, served as middle-man in the north–south trade and connecting the eastern forest of <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> with the western and central <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sudan</a>, the Sahara, and North Africa. The Yoruba manufactured cloth, ironware, and pottery, which were exchanged for salt, leather, and most importantly horses from the Sudan to maintain the cavalry. Oyo remained strong for two hundred years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991173–174_257-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson1991173–174-257">[257]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> It became a protectorate of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a> in 1888, before further fragmenting into warring factions. The Oyo state ceased to exist as any sort of power in 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Benin">Benin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Benin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Benin#History" title="Kingdom of Benin">Kingdom of Benin § History</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Oba_of_Benin" title="Oba of Benin">Oba of Benin</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2150" data-file-width="1610" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg/180px-Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg/270px-Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg/360px-Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benin_bronze_Louvre_A97-14-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Benin Bronze" (brass)</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Kwa_languages" title="Kwa languages">Kwa</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niger%E2%80%93Congo" title="Niger–Congo">Niger–Congo</a> speaking <a href="/wiki/Edo_people" title="Edo people">Edo people</a> had established the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">Benin Empire</a> by the middle of the 15th century. It was engaged in political expansion and consolidation from its very beginning. Under <i>Oba</i> (king) <a href="/wiki/Ewuare" title="Ewuare">Ewuare</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1450</span> – 1480 AD), the state was organized for conquest. He solidified central authority and initiated 30 years of war with his neighbors. At his death, the Benin Empire extended to <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">Dahomey</a> in the west, to the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a> in the east, along the west African coast, and to the Yoruba towns in the north.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ewuare's grandson <i>Oba</i> <a href="/wiki/Esigie" title="Esigie">Esigie</a> (1504–1550) eroded the power of the <i>uzama</i> (state council) and increased contact and trade with Europeans, especially with the Portuguese who provided a new source of copper for court art.
The <i>oba</i> ruled with the advice of the <i>uzama</i>, a council consisting of chiefs of powerful families and town chiefs of different guilds. Later its authority was diminished by the establishment of administrative dignitaries. Women wielded power. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_mothers_(Africa)" title="Queen mothers (Africa)">queen mother</a> who produced the future <i>oba</i> wielded immense influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup>
</p><p>Benin was never a significant exporter of slaves, as Alan Ryder's book Benin and the Europeans showed. By the early 18th century, it was wrecked with dynastic disputes and civil wars. However, it regained much of its former power in the reigns of Oba Eresoyen and Oba Akengbuda. After the 16th century, Benin mainly exported pepper, ivory, gum, and cotton cloth to the Portuguese and Dutch who resold it to other African societies on the coast. In 1897, the British sacked the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Niger_Delta_and_Igbo">Niger Delta and Igbo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Niger Delta and Igbo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people#History" title="Igbo people">Igbo people § History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bonny#Early_history" title="Kingdom of Bonny">Kingdom of Bonny § Early history</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalabari_Kingdom#History" title="Kalabari Kingdom">Kalabari Kingdom § History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Warri#History" title="Kingdom of Warri">Kingdom of Warri § History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nri#History" title="Kingdom of Nri">Kingdom of Nri § History</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Nri" title="List of rulers of Nri">List of rulers of Nri</a></div>
<div class="floatright noresize" role="img" style="width: 400px; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Igboland.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="2933" decoding="async" height="314" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Igboland.png/400px-Igboland.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Igboland.png/600px-Igboland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Igboland.png/800px-Igboland.png 2x" width="400"/></a>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:222px; top:208px"><a href="/wiki/Aba,_Nigeria" title="Aba, Nigeria">Aba</a></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:166px; top:128px"><a href="/wiki/Ihiala" title="Ihiala">Ihiala</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:238px; top:144px"><a href="/wiki/Okigwe" title="Okigwe">Okigwe</a></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:178px; top:168px"><a href="/wiki/Owerri" title="Owerri">Owerre</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:90px; top:128px"><a href="/wiki/Obiaruku" title="Obiaruku">Obiaruku</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:94px; top:76px"><a href="/wiki/Agbor" title="Agbor">Agbor</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:106px; top:176px"><a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River"><span style="color: #48A3B5; font-size: 11px; font-style: italic;">Niger <br/>River</span></a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:166px; top:268px"><b><a href="/wiki/Port_Harcourt" title="Port Harcourt">Ugwu Ọcha</a></b></div>
